<div id="review_842920113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/842920113" />
    <a title="Andrea Eliza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9847310-andrea-eliza"><img alt="Andrea Eliza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595966788p2/9847310.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/842920113?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea Eliza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea Eliza" href="/user/show/9847310-andrea-eliza">Andrea Eliza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142411551" href="/book/show/3416385-when-it-happens">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9847310-andrea-eliza?shelf=i-own-this">i-own-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9847310-andrea-eliza?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9847310-andrea-eliza?shelf=no-just-no">no-just-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9847310-andrea-eliza?shelf=bland-mc">bland-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9847310-andrea-eliza?shelf=i-cant-handle-all-your-whining">i-cant-handle-all-your-whining</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9847310-andrea-eliza?shelf=hello-insta-love">hello-insta-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9847310-andrea-eliza?shelf=duel-or-multi-pov">duel-or-multi-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9847310-andrea-eliza?shelf=ugly-covers">ugly-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer842920113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10892775642245755036"><i>
  <blockquote>"There's just... this intensity... something real."</blockquote>
</i><br/>This book is a love story. <b>An insta-love story</b>. And if you don't already know this... I am not a fan of insta-love.<br/><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>"I peer into my dresser drawer at my ancient underwear. If I were seeing my underwear for the first time, what would I think? It all looks kind of damaged. Do I need to get new underwear? I hate having to ask my mom to buy it for me. Everyone wears underwear, but it's humiliating to admit this fact to your mother. Even if she</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText10892775642245755036" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>"There's just... this intensity... something real."</blockquote>
</i><br />This book is a love story. <b>An insta-love story</b>. And if you don't already know this... I am not a fan of insta-love.<br /><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"I peer into my dresser drawer at my ancient underwear. If I were seeing my underwear for the first time, what would I think? It all looks kind of damaged. Do I need to get new underwear? I hate having to ask my mom to buy it for me. Everyone wears underwear, but it's humiliating to admit this fact to your mother. Even if she does do laundry. Suddenly I have a profound idea. I can buy my own underwear!"</blockquote>
</i><br />Meet Tobey. He is a slacker. He is a good-for-nothing musician rocker dude. He clearly doesn't give a shit about high school or college. All he cares about is his music,his band,and Sara. Oh, and don't forget... <b>he is a guy</b>.<br /><br />I had to remind myself of this fact over and over because his POV sounds like a girl through and through. I think the author's idea of making him a "realistic boy" was sprinkling in the f-word and thoughts of sex. But that didn't convince me. He simply sounded like a girl who liked to swear and who thought about sex. Which is not at all unusual. <br /><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"Here's the thing: I want to reinvent myself this year. I've been a nerd since forever. My life for the past three years has been the same tired routine. Same honors classes with the same set of ten kids, same endless piles of homework, same waking up the next day to do it all over again. I'm tired of waiting for my life to begin. Something has to happen. Like an amazing boy. I know he's out there. I just have to find him.</blockquote>
</i><br />Meet the girl Tobey is in love with: Sara. Sara is a super-smart, genius girl. She is a senior in high school,(like Tobey) but to be honest, Sara sounds like a giggly, naive 13 year old girl. And man, there were so many things that I did not like about her.<br /><br /><b>She's controlling, un-supportive, and a total dream-killer:</b><br /><i>
  <blockquote>Sara:"Why are you slacking again?"<br />Tobey:"I'm not!"<br />Sara:"I know about the English paper."<br />Tobey:"We had extra practice this week."<br />Sara:"You're forgetting about your priorities."<br />Tobey: "But the band's taking off again..."<br />Sara:"Everybody's in a band! Don't you get it?...Sorry to be the one to tell you, but there aren't many job opportunities for starving artists. Unless you like being a waiter."<br />Tobey:"Don't you think I'm good?"<br />Sara:"You know I do. But it doesn't matter what I think."<br />Tobey:"I have dreams,too, Sara. Just because they're not the same as yours doesn't make them less important."<br />Sara:"I'm not saying they are. But college needs to be your priority."</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>She is the queen of slut-shaming:</b><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"Did he used to go out with her? She's such a skanky ho-bag!"</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>She is the queen of jealousy:</b><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"I've been trying to be okay with the fact that there was another girl in Tobey's bed before me. And I've been trying to be okay with the fact that Tobey's first time wasn't with me. But I'm not okay with the fact that he won't tell me who she was. Or anything about her."</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Don't even get me started on how <b>she called her own boyfriend a "man-whore"</b> because he casually slept with one girl before her.<br /><br />She makes no sense to me. At one part she tells Tobey to give her space and not to bother her, but then gets pissed off that he never calls her. Basically, <b>she's pissed at him for respecting her own wishes</b>. I'm glad she is looking for a guy who has no respect for her wishes. *Round of Applause* <br /><br />And despite the issues I had with characters and the story, I also did not like the writing. I didn't think there was much to it. It was simplistic and lack-luster, which isn't always a bad thing, but in this case it was. At times, I even found it painful to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10892775642245755036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_135415518" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135415518" />
    <a title="Natshane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3422972-natshane"><img alt="Natshane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491838445p2/3422972.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135415518?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natshane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natshane" href="/user/show/3422972-natshane">Natshane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer135415518&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135415518" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12755135895006870334">My exact thoughts were 'Is there actually a guy out there like Tobey?'<br/>I always have gotten used to the idea of guys being un-romantic and incapable of well, passion that every time when I read a book about a guy professing his undying love to his 'soul mate', I'm taken aback. In my mind, guys are so insensitive, and that had me wondering if the fictional characters in the book is actually a rare image of reality-living-guys. So, back to the book, does a guy like Tobey really do exist? It's a wid</span>
  <span id="freeText12755135895006870334" style="display:none">My exact thoughts were 'Is there actually a guy out there like Tobey?'<br />I always have gotten used to the idea of guys being un-romantic and incapable of well, passion that every time when I read a book about a guy professing his undying love to his 'soul mate', I'm taken aback. In my mind, guys are so insensitive, and that had me wondering if the fictional characters in the book is actually a rare image of reality-living-guys. So, back to the book, does a guy like Tobey really do exist? It's a wide world....<br /><br />Tobey sort of reminds me of Edward Cullen, him being so in love with Sara and all, I mean, he's not like other made-up guys I've read before in books! (Apart from Edward Cullen, but he's a vampire so....) He is so emotionally involved with Sara that hearing the word I Love You made me widened my eyes. At first, the way Tobey is so obsessed with Sara sort of warms me yet creeped me out a little, but it's so predictable and cliche that Tobey and Sara would end up together-in a good way, or else I wouldn't even pick them up, I hate bad endings. So here's 10 things I love about this book.<br /><br />1. Awesome story plot, yes it's sort of typical but at the same time you would find something uncliche in it, which makes you have an emotional outburst. <br /><br />2. It makes me believe that there is a soul mate out there for me (cheesy?) and there is someone like Tobey. I know we are supposed to be able to differentiate between reality and fantasy, after all books are a form of entertainment, but hey, it offers hope too, haha. <br /><br />3. I laughed at Tobey and Mike's friendship, how he is his dating guru, they shared a unique and funny bond, so I finally know what guys talk about, ha!<br /><br />4. Is it possible to not fall head over heels with the relationship Tobey and Sara shared? <br /><br />5. I'm totally engrossed in the story. <br /><br />6. It's so predictable yet so unpredictable at the same time! When Tobey told Sara about he's 'temporal' infatuation towards Cynthia for the use of her....'body', the cliche thing she would do is freak out, which she did. And for even more cliche-ness, she would say stuff like 'I don't want to be with you.' 'You're not who I thought you were' 'We have nothing in common.' BS but instead she took the uncliche route, oh boy did she got mad, but then Tobey didn't have to come begging for her, she accepted so cooly, which surprises me. And how Tobey knows her so well, it's the sweetest thing in the world when you know someone knows you more than you know yourself. <br /><br />7. The little things are the most important and significant piece of the bigger picture. I learned that from the book.<br /><br />8. The writing, the way the story is narrated in both boy and girl's POV (Tobey and Sara), it's like reading both sides of the story at the same time, to know what the characters are thinking and analysing, that was intriguing.<br /><br />9. Overall of this book made me realize the importance of friendship.<br /><br />10. It got me screaming, dancing around, hyperventilating, pumping on my bed, hugging my cowie (My stufedf animal! Girls like stuffed animals okay.) and talking to myself, acting like a total maniac, and that is how I judge a good book. Two things, if it managed to make me go 'unresponsive-1 star' 'falling asleep-2 stars' 'acting unusually-3 stars', 'nuts-4stars' 'haywire-5stars' I'll rate it according to those, and it must be meaningful, deep I supposed but not necessarily extremely deep. Just not that kind of 'I'm a nerd then I turned into Miss Popular then all the guys notices me and that's my senior year story' stuff though, at ;east have some moral values in it, haha. <br /><br />Since I had done the above actions, which proved that my brain nerves are severely impaired-nearing the about to fuse stage, I guess I'll go and rate this five stars huh? <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12755135895006870334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/16318973-chelsea">Chelsea</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16318973-chelsea?shelf=worst-books-ever-published">worst-books-ever-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16318973-chelsea?shelf=books-i-read-in-2013">books-i-read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16318973-chelsea?shelf=not-worth-reading">not-worth-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16318973-chelsea?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer673757266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer370643061966919936">When I finished, I sat on my bed and just thought. There were so many 5 star ratings and people gushing about how good it was, did I somehow miss it? <br/><br/>I'm not understanding what people are finding so "undeniably cute" about this book. I can honestly say, this was one of the worst books I have ever read. <br/><br/>It's not hard to please me. Give me a relatable main character who I will like and a good main guy, and I'm all into the story. <br/><br/>*SPOILER ALERT*<br/><br/>My problems began with Sara and her friends. Supposed</span>
  <span id="freeText370643061966919936" style="display:none">When I finished, I sat on my bed and just thought. There were so many 5 star ratings and people gushing about how good it was, did I somehow miss it? <br /><br />I'm not understanding what people are finding so "undeniably cute" about this book. I can honestly say, this was one of the worst books I have ever read. <br /><br />It's not hard to please me. Give me a relatable main character who I will like and a good main guy, and I'm all into the story. <br /><br />*SPOILER ALERT*<br /><br />My problems began with Sara and her friends. Supposedly they are all best friends, but I only saw the friendship revolving around Sara. They would only talk about Sara's relationship, Sara's problems, Sara's crush. Um one girl's parents got divorced and Sara wanted to talk about losing her virginity. <br /><br />My problems don't end there with her. She is constantly reminding herself that she is smart. Now I consider myself a fairly smart person but you don't hear me telling people that all the freaking time. I swear, she chants it to herself. She even mentions in the beginning that one of her friends isn't as smart as her. I'm over here like, damn bitch! What's your problem?<br /><br /> Even though she's smart, she still can't break up with a guy she knows things aren't working out. Tobey practically forces her!<br /><br />Which brings me to my second problem, a stereotypical slacker. He is emotional, smart but won't admit it, in a band, has a totally don't care vibe and he's sensitive. Swoon!<br /><br />No. <br /><br />Tobey annoyed the hell out of me. I was hoping him and Cynthia would hook up and then everyone would shut up and die. Tobey would not stop obsessing over having sex with Sara!<br /><br />This is the part that makes me really mad: Even though Dave is using so he can lose his virginity to her so everything won't be a lie, we are supposed to hate him for that while cheer Tobey on after he makes disgusting comments. Tobey throws out all his fantasies of sleeping with Sara and it honestly made me sick to watch Sara think he was 'the one'.<br /><br />I'm not saying guys don't think about that, but Tobey was painted as this really sensitive guy. He mentions that and so does Sara. So when he talks that way, I get....confused(?). At least he shut up after they slept together. <br /><br />And all their fights were problems with, guess who? Sara! Then Tobey had to do damage control. Just one I'd like to see a fight like this:<br /><br />Sara: I'm like, so smart!<br />Tobey: Could you stop saying that? It makes me feel bad about myself sometimes. <br />Sara: Then get smarter like me!<br />Tobey: ....<br /><br />My last problem is the structure of this story. Sara sometimes tells her point of view as a story. That's fine, but sometimes she switches randomly to the present. Or the fact that she says 'like' all the time. I'm like, she's like, they're like, whatever. <br /><br />Oh wait, the best part is the simple sentences. <br />For example:<br /><br />They laugh. I laugh. Everyone laughs. <br /><br />How did this get published?! I'm sorry for making this so long, but I'm shocked people like this book. To be honest, I'm tossing this book in the trash. Not worth the dollar I paid at a bookstore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="370643061966919936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12985269789263462220">First of all, i gave this a 1 star at first...but then I changed it because I finished the book. I am very confident that if a book was a 1 star book I would not have finished it HOWEVER this is the only book that I can remember reading and thinking the whole time "...only ____ more pages until this thing is finally over". this is the only young adult book that I have read and thought, man, maybe i', too old for these books. I am well aware that these books are intended for YOUNG adults but gene</span>
  <span id="freeText12985269789263462220" style="display:none">First of all, i gave this a 1 star at first...but then I changed it because I finished the book. I am very confident that if a book was a 1 star book I would not have finished it HOWEVER this is the only book that I can remember reading and thinking the whole time "...only ____ more pages until this thing is finally over". this is the only young adult book that I have read and thought, man, maybe i', too old for these books. I am well aware that these books are intended for YOUNG adults but genernally they are somewhat relatable regardless of age, especially in my case where I am only 23, however, I thought this book was very immature and the writing, to me, was awful.<br /><br />I will first start off by saying what in the world was Susane Colasanti thinking when she decided to use phrases such as "and I was like..." "and so I go...". Now I understand that when you are having a coversation you may use sayings as such but seriously when reading phrases like "he said..." "she said..." work perfectly fine. I found that the choices of phrases really were distracting in this book.<br /><br />The second issue that I had with this book was the alternating POV's. I LOVE when authors give the opportunity to see different POV's, however, only if it is done correctly (i.e Perfect Chemistry Series by Simone Elkeles **must read!**). In this book we had to re-live EVERY scene twice. There was no realy change in the POV's it was literally reading the same thing just changing characters. Everytime I read a chapter that I was not a fan of (basically every other one) I was dreading the next because I knew that I was going to have to re-read it all over again.<br /><br />The third issue is Tobey. I did not find him "swoon-wothy" like others. I guess I must have missed that. I got so annoyed with all his thoughts going back to sex. I mean seriously, romance is a big part of most books but this one just got annoying.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12985269789263462220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8356684240254296338">Like other books, i wanted to read this just for its pretty cover <s> very likely of me. haha </s><br/><br/>Basically, this one is a very fun, fresh and witty read. Since i'm a big sucker for happy endings I love love stories like this. What i trully like about this one is how it is told in both the perspectives of the main characters <i> Sara & Tobey </i> regarding the same situations. The scenes between these two are so sweet, romantic and well-written. I especially like the remake of the scene from <i> Say Anything </i>, w</span>
  <span id="freeText8356684240254296338" style="display:none">Like other books, i wanted to read this just for its pretty cover <s> very likely of me. haha </s><br /><br />Basically, this one is a very fun, fresh and witty read. Since i'm a big sucker for happy endings I love love stories like this. What i trully like about this one is how it is told in both the perspectives of the main characters <i> Sara &amp; Tobey </i> regarding the same situations. The scenes between these two are so sweet, romantic and well-written. I especially like the remake of the scene from <i> Say Anything </i>, wherein Tobey stands in front of Sara's window holding a boombox above his head! <s> kilig.haha.k.</s> The dialogues are fun and very easy-going, typical for high-school couples.<br /><br />This book is not all about happiness and love throughout. There are parts where it wasn’t all lovey-dovey and serious matters were faced. Although it is very predictable and you can tell how the story would go, it is still fun to see that some of your predictions might be wrong. <br /><br />After reading it, i find myself thinking Sara &amp; Tobey was really meant to be, and before i drown to the unconsciousness state of sleeping the last thing on my mind was <i> "I wish I have that something <b> real </b> too."</i><br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristy" href="/user/show/2705039-kristy">Kristy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer682753504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17230859471575816916">Sara is on a quest her senior year; to find something real and to get into NYU. She is a self-described nerd and proud of it, yet secretly longs for popularity and acceptance.<br/><br/>Tobey comes across as a lazy, but musically talented guy. I sort of picture him as a skater boy. He is majory crushing on Sara and even with his gorgeous eyes, he just can't figure out how to get her to notice him. There is the whole problem of Dave, seriously his nickname sould be D-Bag Dave.<br/><br/>Sara, for whatever reason think</span>
  <span id="freeText17230859471575816916" style="display:none">Sara is on a quest her senior year; to find something real and to get into NYU. She is a self-described nerd and proud of it, yet secretly longs for popularity and acceptance.<br /><br />Tobey comes across as a lazy, but musically talented guy. I sort of picture him as a skater boy. He is majory crushing on Sara and even with his gorgeous eyes, he just can't figure out how to get her to notice him. There is the whole problem of Dave, seriously his nickname sould be D-Bag Dave.<br /><br />Sara, for whatever reason thinks Dave is it. She pines for him over summer and when he finally asks her out, she thinks he is amazing. But, after that newlywed phase wears off, she realizes he is not all that great of a guy. But, there just happens to be one right in front of her in music class.<br /><br />3 stars.<br /><br />Very cute, coming of age story. Sweet little romance. Definitely for the older, young adult reader as there is a lot of sexual references and moments going on. Don't get me wrong, it's really mild, but I wouldn't feel comfortable if my say, 13 year old daughter was reading this one. <br /><br />If you're into chik-lit, this is probably for you :)<br /><br />P.S. I love the notes the girls would pass back and forth with famous couples names, i.e. pokey and gumby; wallace and grommit, etc.<br /></span>

<div id="review_92928031" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92928031" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572125481p2/3283298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92928031?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=16-chick-lit">16-chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92928031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12442288932603711965">Hmm, can’t say that I’m very fond of this one. I thought the whole plot was really lame. No twists and turns, no dramatic events or anything like that. While reading I kept thinking “this can’t be it, something must happen soon” and I was always waiting for the big climax. I was still waiting for it on the last page….<br/>What I found extremely annoying was the style of writing. All this “and then I was like and then she goes” wasn’t my thing at all. What’s wrong with good old “I said and she replied</span>
  <span id="freeText12442288932603711965" style="display:none">Hmm, can’t say that I’m very fond of this one. I thought the whole plot was really lame. No twists and turns, no dramatic events or anything like that. While reading I kept thinking “this can’t be it, something must happen soon” and I was always waiting for the big climax. I was still waiting for it on the last page….<br />What I found extremely annoying was the style of writing. All this “and then I was like and then she goes” wasn’t my thing at all. What’s wrong with good old “I said and she replied”? Whenever I read these kind of books (High School love stories) I keep comparing them to my favorite book in this category: Perfect Chemistry. So far, I haven’t found a book that came even remotely close to PC. When It Happens didn’t accomplish this task either.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12442288932603711965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EcWKWsPfDh7T/xLioVUvhJ/zltwvT80NN0VclyDqUTcLDVSxjgCQVHMhEL77tJAqn4KQhkOfFCFLKCDFinRfeg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DieGXp7nTcKc0R3YneUnixC/5y/o5yNB1X26JCxoJqsU71i10zjTiDwPH4THBJglEM7hdYQ3+m2pEMZ2hvYo5g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer15336190123097968189">Susane Colasanti is the bestselling author of <i>When It Happens</i>, <i>Take Me There</i>, <i>Waiting for You</i>, <i>Something Like Fate</i>, <i>So Much Closer</i>, <i>Keep Holding On</i>, <i>All I Need</i>, <i>Now and Forever</i>, and the City Love trilogy.   <span id="freeText15336190123097968189" style="display:none">Susane Colasanti is the bestselling author of <i>When It Happens</i>, <i>Take Me There</i>, <i>Waiting for You</i>, <i>Something Like Fate</i>, <i>So Much Closer</i>, <i>Keep Holding On</i>, <i>All I Need</i>, <i>Now and Forever</i>, and the City Love trilogy. She has a bachelor’s degree from the University of Pennsylvania and a master’s degree from New York University. Before becoming a full-time author in 2007, Susane was a high school science teacher for ten years. She lives in New York City. <br /><br />You can connect with Susane on her <a href="http://www.facebook.com/susanecolasantibooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>, <a href="http://twitter.com/susanecolasanti" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>, <a href="http://www.youtube.com/user/susanecolasanti" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a>, <a href="http://colasantibooks.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a>, and <a href="https://instagram.com/susanecolasanti" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15336190123097968189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
